< Review>
This is my first and only Google review, which should be a ZERO.

I've been a MINI loyalist since 2016 and have had incredible service from MINI dealers in three other states until attempting to lease a vehicle from MINI Santa Monica.  I was talking with Sam in Sales for a couple weeks about finding and leasing a vehicle in what should have been a straight-forward transaction with very little guess work.  I was in the process of relocating and splitting my time between two locations and unfortunately could not meet in person, which of course is ideal.

Nevertheless, Sam set the expectation that the dealer would run my financing, make me an offer and, if agreed, I would come to the dealer to sign paperwork as soon as I could, which was in 5 days.  He arrogantly proclaimed, "I've put vehicles on hold for people for up to 2 weeks; it's no problem at all."  He also promised he would FedEx my lease paperwork due to the long distance so I anticipated the hard part would be over before I arrived to the dealer to pick up my vehicle in 5 days ... WRONG.

Sam sent me an application via email and when I decided on a vehicle, I returned my completed application with a copy of my drivers license PER HIS REQUEST.  I waited almost 5 hours before calling the dealership back trying to track down Sam and ask for status on his promises.  Nothing but the run-around from other staff and direct to his voicemail.

Why on Earth would a car salesman dodge a buyer's phone calls??

After getting a sudden cold shoulder from Sam after submitting my application, I left an urgent message with Seth, the Sales manager, stating it was almost the end of the day on a Friday before a holiday weekend and MINI Financial Services was already closed for consumers. I mean, who wants to drag out car buying any longer than absolutely necessary? Sam then FINALLY returned my call and ACTED LIKE A COMPLETELY DIFFERENT PERSON.

He reneged on running my electronic credit application, which made it completely unethical for him to ask for it in the first place.  He reneged on holding the vehicle until I could physically be at the dealer to sign paperwork.  Not only did he renege on every single promise, he became UNHINGED when I held him accountable.  He literally began SCREAMING at me like it was a domestic dispute.  He went from professional and accommodating to taking everything personally and becoming abusive toward me when his gaslighting tactics didn't work.

Sadly, when I asked Seth to step in, it was more chauvinistic behavior, an outright denial of wrong-doing, and a blatant refusal to make this process seamless for me in any way possible.  He even called me by another woman's name ... WHO IS ELIZABETH??  I later received a half-a$$ apology from Seth followed by, "Can we just move on?," without even letting me express my concerns.  I had to rearrange my busy holiday weekend to ACCOMODATE THEM.  I was lured, baited, switched, then swiftly discarded even when I held my end of the deal, which ultimately led to a complete violation of my privacy and unethical business practices.  If the dealer asserts one cannot purchase a vehicle electronically in CA, then stop asking for personal information like SSN and drivers license VIA EMAIL and making fake promises to "see if the customer is committed" then not follow through with the sale.

The way these guys talk to women and people of color is absolutely horrific.  Clearly the promises that were broken for me were previously honored for "other customers."  While I still love the MINI brand, I will never forget this humiliating experience as long as I live and will never return to or recommend this dealer.</Review>

< Text>
Having just moved back to CA from overseas, my family and I were in need of a car quickly. I contacted MINI of Santa Monica and was immediately introduced to Mike. Mike was extremely knowledgeable and professional; he showed me every car I asked about. He had no hidden agenda - he was simply there to help, answering all questions with thoughtful and detailed answers. I told Mike I'd discuss the options with my wife and Mike NEVER asked for my phone number or email before I left the dealership. This, in itself, was incredibly telling as every other dealership I'd been to had jumped me for my personal details as if I had the word "lead" tattooed to my forehead. I called Mike the next day and unfortunately he was out sick. Instead of asking if I could come in a day or two later, he put me in immediate contact with Rich, who Mike said was "equally or even more knowledgeable about Minis than I am." Sure enough, when I met with Rich that day, he had the same professional and low key manner. Like Mike, he was most interested in making sure my questions were answered, and less interested in whether or not I purchased a vehicle from him. And like Mike, he loves these cars - so everything he showed me felt extremely personal to him. At the risk of sounding overly corny, it was like Rich owned Mini, the company, and was proud of what he'd created. Needless to say, within two hours of walking in, I was driving away in my new car. The next day I received an excited call from Rich, asking me about my drive back to Malibu in my new Mini. You see, I had never requested a test drive which says it all....<//Text>

I couldn't have had a more positive experience selecting and leasing my new MINI than I did at MINI of Santa Monica, largely due to my incredibly personable and refreshingly straightforward salesman, Mauricio Ortega. Mauricio was an absolute pleasure to deal with from the moment I walked in to the moment I drove away in my awesome 2019 Starlight Blue MINI. I've never met a car salesman I liked so much -- Mauricio is smart, caring and interested in making sure his customers are happy. He never uses any of the high-pressure techniques car salesmen are notorious for, and talking with him felt like having a conversation with a friend. After he patiently showed me the cars in the dealership and went through my options with me, he found the exact car I was looking for (which was not at the dealership -- he actually found me two options, a 2019 and a 2020) and even called me on his day off to let me know the car was mine. This exemplifies the kind of attentive service that goes above and beyond that I got from Mauricio at every step of the process. When it was time to negotiate and sign my lease, Mauricio didn't subject me to the typical back and forth but went straight to the best offer, which was actually hard to believe. This is my third MINI but my first time at MINI of Santa Monica, and the first time I enjoyed the process of getting the car as much as driving it.<//Review>

<user_id>106862607446239956160</user_id>< Name>
Venkatesh Venkataramanan</Name>
<Time>1600140771143</Time>< Rating>

< review>
I went to Singh Law firm for my estate planning needs after I read about their Yelp and Google reviews. While some aspects of it is true, there are many aspects where they fell short with my expectations.

The Positives:

1. They are very responsive , professional and courteous.
2. Mr Singh took the time to walk us thru' the process and what to expect in the same.
3. The front desk can assist with most queries and advice.
4. They are well organized and follow up promptly via email when you have questions.

The Negatives:

1. They are extremely inflexible and can be perceived as rude when you have situations that need them to tailor their approach. As you are aware, the process requires that you notarize documents. Given the current CoVID situation, I was hesitant to visit their offices (I live with elderly folks in my home). So I asked them if there were other options. All I was told there was none. I spent a multiple hours researching online and found that California allows online notarizations if you are able to get it done from notaries in states that recognize online notarizations. When I asked them about it, I was told that their policy is that I sign in their offices. After exchanging half a dozen or more emails on this topic wherein I cited links to multiple sites that indicated that this was acceptable did the firm acknowledge the availability of the same but still strongly recommended I visit their offices. After a few more emails, on the topic Mr Singh agreed to take a phone call. He said while this is allowed, he wasn't in a position to provide any guidance on the topic and that I would be doing it assuming all the risk. I later learnt that this idea of getting notarized online is being recommended and followed by every other firm that does this kind of work except them. To me this wasn't what I expected from a law firm if they care for the well being of the customer.

2. This is yet another example how rigid the firm gets when unanticipated things occur in the process. Soon after I got my documents completed, I decided to take advantage of the low interest rates to refinance my home. In all transparency, I had no plans of refinancing the home at the time I was going through this process. Neither was it made clear AT ANY POINT in the process (documents or such) that I should hold off on any kind of refinancing till the process completes. When the question of  title holder on the property came up, I called them to see what I should use since I was told during the signing process that the update to the county records would take 12-15 weeks. The front desk person said that it was OK to go ahead with the refinancing process with the name on the title to be what it is currently since the county processing is going to be longer than closing. I called them again a few weeks later since the refinancing company wanted some clarifications. During the second call, I was told that I should have notified them "before" they started the name transfer and now it is out of their hands and that they have no "advice" for me to provide at this time.  I felt like I was out on a limb. This process is being played out as we speak and I hope it doesn't get things complicated.

In summary, I think the firm may be good if you are able to stick to their rigid guidelines and aren't expecting any flexibility in the process. Also try to use email to communicate with them since you will need if for your "records".<//review>
<Pictures>None<//Pictures><Response>{'time': 1600123957619, 'text': "Thank you for your review Venkatesh. I‚Äôm glad we were able to handle your Estate Planning remotely for your parent‚Äôs safety considering the COVID pandemic.\n\nI‚Äôd like to address the issues you've brought up to bring some clarity to you.\n\n1. California DOES NOT allow for online notarization. Please review the Secretary of State‚Äôs website and analysis on this here:\n\nhttps://www.sos.ca.gov/business-programs/bizfile/covid-19-frequently-asked-questions/\n\nWe did instruct that we cannot comment on another‚Äôs state‚Äôs online notary, as we‚Äôre not notaries of another state (only California). We did instruct you that so long as the online notary you were going to get done (from another state) was done following the rules and regulations of that state‚Äôs notary rules, then the documents would be executed properly for purposes of California.\n\n2. Our staff correctly instructed you that when we submit your deed for recordation with the county recorder‚Äôs office, it could take 10-12 weeks.  Also, if we knew you were going to refinance prior to us submitting your deed, we would have held the deed in our office and let your refi complete prior to submitting. <review>Singh Law Firm was suggested by my company through LegalEASE for my Estate Planning purposes. Here is how the process went:

1. We had a 15 minute phone session with Attorney Kern Singh. The phone question was really brief, I didn‚Äôt get to ask any real questions, and was promised detailed explanations on the day of signing.

2.They sent an email questionnaire that had questions about our preferences, which we filled out.

3. Astonishingly, the next step in the process was the actual signing process, which was scheduled a couple of weeks after.

I don‚Äôt see how one can go from #2 to #3, without any other steps in between!

We had so many questions about the estate planning process and the kind of plan would be best for us.

I would have expected a couple of rounds of back and forth to decide what kind of plan we would need. I would have expected a preview of the plan to be sent to us so that I and my wife could go over it, and if necessary, make modifications.

On the first (and only) first phone call, Attorney Kern Singh promised that all would be explained on the day of signing. Being very new to the process, I agreed to go to the third step of the signing process. I was expecting, based on the phone conversation, some set amount of time on the day of signing, that would be the ‚Äúeducation‚Äù process. In retrospect, I don‚Äôt see how this would have even worked. If we were expecting to sign on that day, how would I even be able to discuss any of this with my wife?

On the day of signing, we found the Attorney ready with a stack of papers for us to sign. They started the process of notarizing us with thumbprints and driver‚Äôs licenses. At this point it became clear that we were just going to go through the signing process! How did they even prepare the documents?? When I pointed out to the Attorney that I was expecting some kind of an education process first, where we will go through what kind of plan we needed, Attorney Kern Singh said that that conversation already happened in the first phone call! I found him to be rude and dismissive.

Again, in retrospect, I am not sure how this process would even have worked. We decided not to sign on that day.

I found another Attorney to do the Estate Plan. This process was everything I had hoped for. Multiple email and phone conversations, early preview of the document, subsequent fine tuning and changing things to our preferences, and then, finally, signing.

I had decided to go to Singh Law Firm seeing all the glowing reviews. But my experience does not match those reviews. Maybe if you need simpler documents, they would do a good job. Maybe the whole Covid-19 situation meant they were too busy. But I don‚Äôt see how something as complex as an Estate Planning process can be done the way they proposed to do it. I didn‚Äôt work for us.</review>< userid>

iSmile came to the bay area last year with a different approach to dentistry & orthodontics. Open office space with huge flat screens in the 20-30 oratories, the whir of hepa - fans in the background give patients the progressive & proactive atmosphere that this is a CLEAN clinic. Well designed & managed with pro-modern investment in cleanliness including 03 or UC-V sterilization & LED lighting, training & professionalism. Their DSP dental savings program saves money annually. At 60 I have 20 teeth left bc parents didn't take kids to dentists in the 70s. After a gentle scaling & cleaning by 1 of their many hygienists, they scan your smile & offer solutions. I decided to invest 5K in a couple implants so I can eat meals in a timely manner. Bc of bone loss I was not eligible for full quadrant implants. But 1 here & 1 there installed expertly by Dr Kim & staff and I enjoy eating again. Life changer! With DSP I saved over 1K this year catching up on my dental health. And got appointments within days. Dont wait, Go for it!<//Review>

We got an ad for them for a promotional combination package including cleaning and x-rays and evaluation. My husband was due for a cleaning but we had just moved, so we didn't have local dental insurance, so we decided to give it a try. Do not recommend this office to anyone.</Review>

She handed me a second milk, which I opened and smelled; it didn't smell very bad, but smelled just off enough for me to consider it spoiled also. The lady called over 2 people who seemed like managers and no one seemed to know what to do. I was offered another milk (after 2 spoiled? Ummm, no thanks).
